SPEAKER'S CERTIFICATE

88 ( ) (The Hon. Deputy Speaker) I wish to inform Parliament that the Hon. Speaker has endorsed the Certificate on the Bill titled Appropriation on 21st March, 2025 in terms of the Provisions of Article 79 of the Constitution of the Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka.

88888) 88

:88 () :

VALUE ADDED TAX (AMENDMENT) BILL: DETERMINATION

OF THE SUPREME COURT 88 ( ) (The Hon. Deputy Speaker) I wish to inform Parliament that the Hon. Speaker has received the Decision of the Supreme Court in respect of the Bill titled Value Added Tax (Amendment), which had been challenged in the Supreme Court in terms of Article 121(1) of the Constitution.

The Supreme Court has communicated that since both Petitioners in S.C. (SD) 05/2025 and S.C. (SD) 06/2025 had opted not to proceed with the matter in view of the undertakings given by the State, the Court had not made a Determination on the Constitutionality of the Bill.

I order that the Decision of the Supreme Court be printed in the Official Report of todays Proceedings.

DEATH OF HON. KOSALA NUWAN JAYAWEERA

88 ( ) (The Hon. Deputy Speaker) I wish to inform this House that a vacancy in the Membership of this Parliament has occurred with effect from the 06th of April, 2025, in terms of the provisions of Article 66(a) of the Constitution due to the death of the Hon. Kosala Nuwan Jayaweera, Member of Parliament of the Electoral District of Kegalle.

It is with profound regret that I inform this Parliament of his passing away. On behalf of Parliament, I would like to convey that we are deeply saddened by his demise and would like to express our heartfelt sympathies to the family of the Hon. Member.

The Vote of Condolence in this regard will be presented to Parliament on a future date.

asked the Minister of Urban Development, Construction and Housing:

(a) Is he aware that -

(i) the project to provide drinking water to Vavuniya Town was implemented during the years 2010-2011 with financial assistance of the Asian Development Bank and that paddy fields, farmlands, houses and religious places were acquired for that purpose;

(ii) a tripartite agreement was signed on 05.11.2013 among the farmers organizations, the Divisional Secretary and the National Water Supply and Drainage Board in this regard so that no prejudice would be caused to the farmers and the land owners;

(iii) issuing of permits for the alternative lands provided in place of the acquired lands, and providing proper irrigation facilities and establishing and renovating access roads for those lands have not been done up until now;

(iv) members of the affected farming families have not been provided with jobs under the above-mentioned water supply project on a priority basis so far; and

(v) no action has been taken to channel the additional water overflowing from the anicuts to the renovated tanks belonging to the Department of Agrarian Development?

(b) If so, will he inform this House of the measures that will be taken to resolve the issues referred to above?

(c) If not, why?

888 ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) Hon. Deputy Speaker, thank you very much for giving me this opportunity. I would like to ask this Question on the impact of the 44 per cent tax on Sri Lankan exports to the United States from the Hon. Minister of Finance.

65 66

Sri Lankas export sector, particularly that of the textile and apparel industry, has long relied on access to the US market as a key driver of economic growth. Given our fragile economic situation and our ongoing recovery from bankruptcy, maintaining stable trade relations with key partners is crucial and is a must for sustaining employment, foreign exchange inflows and overall economic stability.

On 18th March, 2025, I raised a Question in this House under Standing Order No. 27(2) regarding the potential risks posed by the United States' deglobalization policies and the tariff increases on Sri Lankan exports. With those concerns being highlighted well in advance on the 2nd of April, 2025, US President Donald Trump imposed a 44 per cent reciprocal tariff on Sri Lankan imports to the United States. This decision is a severe blow to our export sector, affecting thousands of businesses, workers and overall investor confidence in Sri Lankas economic recovery.

It is imperative that the Government provides clarity on its preparedness, response and future course of action in addressing this critical issue. In that regard, could the Hon. Minister inform this House,

1. Proactive Measures: After I raised this Question on the 18th of March, 2025, what immediate diplomatic or trade- related actions were taken by the Government to prevent such a drastic tariff imposition?

2. Counter-strategies: In response to the newly imposed 44 per cent tax, what short-term and long-term counter-strategies will the Government adopt to protect Sri Lankas export sector, rubber-based items, tea, marine exports (export of fish et cetera) and particularly the textile and apparel industries?

3. Engagement with US Officials: Since my Question was raised, with whom in the US administration, the US Trade Representative (USTR) or other relevant authorities, has the Government engaged in discussions regarding this tariff hike and what has been the outcome of those engagements?

4. Diplomatic Engagements and Negotiations with the US: Given that Sri Lanka is still emerging from bankruptcy, has the Government formally requested President Trump or the US administration to consider a special dispensation or an exemption for Sri Lankan exports?

5. Market Diversification: Given the volatility of the US trade policy, what are the alternative export markets or trade agreements the Government is actively pursuing to reduce Sri Lankas dependence on the US market?

What I am referring to is the future free trade agreements under our market diversification strategy, taking our exports away from the one market that dominates at the moment.

6. Detailed Export Data: Over the past five years, what have been the primary products exported from Sri Lanka to the United States and what has been the export value for each of those products on an annual basis?

7. Tariff Comparisons: What are the current tariff rates imposed by the United States on imports from Sri Lankas main competitors in the textile and apparel sector and specifically on countries such as Indonesia, China, African countries, Vietnam, Bangladesh and India? How do these rates compare with the 44 per cent tariff now imposed on Sri Lankan exports? 8. Strategic Response: Given the competitive disadvantage posed by the higher tariffs on Sri Lankan exports, what are the specific strategies the Government is implementing to enhance the competitiveness of our export sector in the US market? As asked before, I am referring to the interest rates et cetera which have been mentioned here. 9. Support for Exporters: What measures are being taken to support Sri Lankan exporters affected by these tariffs, particularly the small and medium-sized enterprises which may be disproportionately impacted?

Sir, I know this is a national problem. I heard the Leader of the Opposition requesting that we convene an All-Party Conference on this matter. So, let us take this as a national crisis. You would not be able to take the world on. So, let the world pay attention to those particular areas where they are trying to impose taxes in a very capricious manner.

Thank you.

8) 8 0888888888) ( () - ) (The Hon. (Dr.) Anil Jayantha - Minister of Labour and Deputy Minister of Economic Development) Hon. Deputy Speaker, in fact, with regard to the matters raised by this Question, we have been both proactive and reactive, as has been necessary. However, we did not panick and have not been driven by emotions. All the possible risks and consequences have been assessed and taken into consideration, accordingly.

Diplomatic relations and continuous dialogues with the White House and the Office of the US Trade Representative have been taking place continuously. To highlight some of the actions we have taken, diplomatic measures have been taken on 14th February, 2025. The Sri Lankan Ambassador to the United States has engaged with continuous discussions and based on the outcome of those discussions, a particular report had been sent to us, which we have evaluated. Then, there has been another engagement with the International Monetary Fund as well just to highlight the significance of this issue since we are working under an EFF Programme of the IMF. There was another meeting held on Trade Policy Analysis and Strategic Alternatives on 28th March, 2025. At that meeting, the Embassy undertook a comprehensive review of Sri Lankas current import profile from the United States and analysed US export performances globally. It was observed that most of the US goods are already subject to relative para-tariffs, but not other tariffs. Accordingly, some proposals have also been made. Then, on 01st April, 2025, the Sri Lankan Embassy engaged with the Office of the US Trade Representative, in which discussions Mr. Brendan Lynch, Assistant United States Trade Representative for South and Central Asia and Ms.

67 68

[88 8]

2025 08

Emily Ashby, Director for South and Central Asia took part. Immediately responding to the Executive Order of 02nd April, 2025 or once this announcement was made, the particular Report was submitted. So, that is with regard to the diplomatic relations.

Then, the Hon. President of Sri Lanka appointed a Special Committee comprising industry experts, Government officials and the two Deputy Ministers to look into this particular situation and to propose possible actions to be taken. Accordingly, several meetings were conducted locally. And in addition, we also had a virtual discussion with the officials of the Office of the US Trade Representative, where we discussed the possible mitigation options to reduce this trade deficit. Even though it is stated that the tariff rates are very high, the calculation is simply based on the trade deficit divided by its corresponding imports. Therefore, our proposal should also be based on ways and means of reducing this particular gap. So, these things are being discussed and a report is also being prepared. We will be having another virtual meeting with the Office of the US Trade Representative tonight at 8.00 p.m..

Further, we held several roundtable discussions at the Lakshman Kadirgamar Institute well before this particular announcement was made, in which politicians and local experts took part. In addition, the Hon. President also wrote a letter directly to the United States President Donald Trump, highlighting the possible ways of mitigating these things, the actions that we could take and requested for collaboration to reduce these tariffs. That letter has already been presented to the White House and the White House has also acknowledged its receipt.

Therefore, some views that have been spread over social media and the ideas expressed by some people that we have not taken appropriate action are not true; we have taken action. With regard to this particular situation, we have to understand that it is not a situation between only two countries, but a global situation. By the United States, a standard formula has been applied and there is no room for any country to proactively negotiate and get a concession. I will give you two examples. One is India. India went to the United States and had certain discussions about these tariffs, but still their reciprocal tariff rate is 26 per cent. That is, 50 per cent of the trade deficit divided by its total imports of US Dollars 85 billion.

So, it is very clear that it is applied for all the countries. That is example number one. Example number two is this. Before the imposition of these tariffs on 02nd April, The US Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent categorically said, "On April 2, each country will receive a number that we believe..." - I emphasis the word "believe" - "....that represents their tariffs. So, for some countries, it could be quite low; for some countries, it could be quite high." The US Treasury Secretary further highlights that they hope that after the nations receive their reciprocal tariff numbers, they would come to them and would want to negotiate for reductions. So, he very clearly states that negotiations for reduction of tariffs could take place only after this particular announcement would be made.

Now, I want to give some summarized answers for the other questions on market diversification. So, apart from these tariffs -

888 ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) Hon. Deputy Speaker, let me seek a clarification so that he would be able to summarize the -

88 ( ) (The Hon. Deputy Speaker) Could you please wait till the Hon. Minister finishes?

8) 8 0888 ( () ) (The Hon. (Dr.) Anil Jayantha) Yes, first, let me finish; I will finish quickly.

Apart from these measures, as far as the export market is concerned, we have already explored and are still exploring possible market diversifications. We are especially looking for opportunities under GSP Plus in the European region and also possibilities under UK's DCTS. Even in China, the Middle East, India and in other South Asian countries, there are also various possibilities. In addition, we also can enter into special trade agreements as well.

Then, moving on to the detailed import and export data for the last five years, it clearly indicates that our trade deficit with regard to the US is almost 88 per cent, as shown. Out of the items that we export to the United States, 85 per cent accounts for five items including apparels, food items and other main products. Therefore, we basically need to pay attention to those five items. If we take imports from the US, there are food items, pharmaceutical products - of course, for pharmaceutical products, the tariff is zero - turbojets, optical and photographic items and plastic and other related items.

I just mentioned the major categories. On those, the tariff rates are not that much; they vary from zero to 20 per cent, but there are the para-tariffs. That, of course, we can discuss. So, taking into account all these things, our team is exploring ways and means of resolving this issue and we hope we would be able to find a solution for that.

Hon. Deputy Minister, India intervened and changing the trade base that was there, they agreed to ensure that more imports of LNG from the US would come in. What I basically mention at this particular moment is, we cannot take on the policy, but could take practical steps to ensure that the US is given market access at zero duty, which would help us. These are not things, if you bring from one country, which could not be brought from another because the point of origin is not always the country of origin. The goods of the USA could also be bought from Japan, Dubai and Singapore, which are normally their regional bases of manufacturing. Therefore, we should basically go forward and offer a zero-based duty structure as well as an investment climate to the US companies so that we could go into the launching pad of India. That would help our policy. The reason why I basically mention this is that we have 875,000 direct and indirect jobs related to our exports to America. Out of the 11 trillion, 26 per cent is to the US and we, Sri Lankans, handle 0.09 per cent of the world trading.

8 88 8 8 8 8 888.88

Also, at the same, I would like to respond to some of the thoughts that were expressed here. Some said that some provisions are unconstitutional; some others said that this is shifting the burden unfairly. But, Sir, not a single FR case was filed in the Supreme Court against this legislation. 8 8 8 8 8 8 8 0 8 8 8 8 0 8 88 8 8 8 8 8 8 88.8 8888.8

Then, let me explain about the provisions of this Act. The provisions of the Proceeds of Crime Act would not attract Article 13 (6) of the Constitution. That is because, no penal sanctions are to be applied against the possessor when proceeeds of crime are forfeited. All what happens is, the legally acquired property would be returned to the State or to the victims. However, all offences contained in the Bill would only have prospective application, not retrospective application, as suggested. Further, the forfeiture provisions cannot be considered as retrospective penal legislation since forfeiture does not involve imposition of penal sanctions. If the forfeiture provisions are to be applied only prospectively, what will we do with regard to acquisition of property by committing drug trafficking and corruption of the past? 8 8 8 8 8 8 88 8 8 8 8 88 8 8 8 8 8 8 8 8 8 88.8 88 88888 88 88 888.8

Whereupon THE HON. (PROF.) SENA NANAYAKKARA left the Chair, and THE HON. DEPUTY SPEAKER took the Chair.

88888 ( ) (The Hon. Harshana Nanayakkara, Attorney-at-Law) 8 8 8 8 888 8 8 8 8 8 8 8 88 8 8 8 8 8 8 8 888 8.8 8 8888 8 8 8 8 8 8 88 88 .8

Sir, what is the purpose of bringing this law? I heard some submissions being made to say that this law will not work and that there are enough provisions which could deal with stolen assets under the laws already in existance. It is partly true, partly false and partly ignorant. Why? Because this is the only law which allows - in Sri Lanka, almost all the laws are conviction-based, which means that there must be conviction of a person prior to their stolen assets being forfeited - non-conviction-based forfeiture. That is the most important aspect of this legislation. 8 888 88 8888 8.8 8 888888 8888888 8 08 8 8 8 8 88.88 88.888 8 8 8 8 .8 8 8 8 8 8 proceeds of crime 8 8 8 8.888 88 88 8888 88 888888.8I will read a portion of the Report of the Committee to Develop the Policy and Legal Framework and Draft Provisions of the Proposed Law on Proceeds of Crime, which drafted this legislation. Let me quote from page 27 of that Report:

In the traditional sense, proceeds of crime are referred to as fruits of crime. The present law of Sri Lanka provides in certain circumstances for such fruits of crime to be forfeited or returned to the relevant victims of crime. In terms of the existing law, forfeiture of proceeds of crime can take place sequel to the conviction of a person for having committed the offence, which yielded the relevant proceeds of crime. This mechanism is referred to as conviction-based forfeiture of proceeds of crime or as post-conviction forfeiture of proceeds of crime. Criminal justice professionals are aware that forfeiture of proceeds of crime (as opposed to equipment, vehicles, utensils, weapons, etc. used to commit crime) following conviction of offenders is a very rare occurrence and is an extremely difficult goal to achieve. The Committee observed a lack of focus in the present law relating to proceeds of crime, which is manifest by the glaring fact that the Code of Criminal Procedure Act, No. 15 of 1979 does not even make a reference to proceeds of crime.

Sir, let me now thank those Committee members who contributed to this amazing piece of work. Actually, I would like to tell their names: Hon. Justice Yasantha Kodagoda, President's Counsel and Judge of the Supreme Court, was the Chairman of the Committee; Mr. Rohantha Abeysuriya, President's Counsel and Additional Solicitor General, Attorney-Generals Department; Mr. Kuvera de Zoysa, President's Counsel; Mr. Sarath Jayamanne, President's Counsel and former Director of the Commission to Investigate Allegations of Bribery or Corruption; Mr. Neville Abeyratne, President's Counsel; Mr. Priyantha Nawana, President's Counsel; Mr. Sanjaya Gamage, Attorney-at-Law; Mr. Sudarshana De Silva, Senior Deputy Solicitor General, Attorney-Generals Department, to whom I am very grateful because, even today, he is in the Officials' Box assisting me in presenting this legislation. Thank you very much, Hon. Attorney-General. The other members of the Committee are, Mr. Amal A. Randeniya, Attorney-at-Law; Dr. Ayesh Ariyasinghe, Additional Director, Financial Intelligence Unit, Central Bank of Sri Lanka; Mr. Asanga Karawita, Attorney-at-Law; Mr. Kamal Silva, Attorney-at-Law; Ms. Disna Gurusinghe, Assistant Director General, Commission to Investigate Allegations of Bribery or Corruption. As the Minister of Justice, I place on record my sincere

Sir, I think I have answered all of the questions that were raised during the speeches that were made. Therefore, finally, what I would like to say at this moment of passing this piece of legislation is that it is a historical moment.

888 . . Question proposed. 888.888 ( . ) (The Hon. M. Nizam Kariapper, PC) Hon. Deputy Speaker, - 88 ( ) (The Hon. Deputy Speaker) Yes, Hon. Kariapper?

888.888 ( . ) (The Hon. M. Nizam Kariapper, PC) Thank you very much, Sir.

I once again reiterate Standing Order No. 91. (f). for the purpose of my point of Order. It states, I quote:

No Member shall refer in any motion or debate, to any matter which is under adjudication by a court of law

Unfortunately, the fourth paragraph of the Sinhala version of this Resolution appearing on page 10 of todays Order Paper contains Supreme Court cases still pending. Then, incident Nos. 1 to 16 in the Resolution contain pending murder cases. So, as it now constitutes, this Resolution violates Standing Order No. 91. (f) and will also give an opportunity for the person concerned to raise an objection in the appropriate court that he had not got a fair trial because he had been tried by a committee. On top of that, this Committee is going to consist a Supreme Court Judge, before whom those Supreme Court cases are still pending. Therefore, I humbly request that we make appropriate amendments to the Resolution. I am very keen to have this Resolution on the removal of Deshabandu Tennakoon proceeded with, but with proper amendments.

Thank you very much. 88 ( ) (The Hon. Deputy Speaker) Hon. Kariapper, I would like to inform you that this matter had already been brought to the notice of the Committee on Parliamentary Business held on 02nd April, 2025 by some Members of Parliament representing the Opposition. Their concern that the Resolution is sub judice was considered by the Committee on Parliamentary Business and at the request of those Members of the Opposition, the Hon. Speaker agreed to record those concerns in the Minutes of that Meeting. Since the Committee on Parliamentary Business is

mandated with deciding on the Business of Parliament, the Committee decided to schedule the Resolution for Business of Parliament on Tuesday, 08th April, 2025, which is today. Therefore, there is no necessity of raising this matter at this moment.

Does the House agree to Item No. 3?
